<div id="review_246612592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246612592" />
    <a title="Marika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5719841-marika"><img alt="Marika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326063085p2/5719841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246612592?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marika" href="/user/show/5719841-marika">Marika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246612592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5732395905757136378">Galaxy Craze's new YA is set, like many YA these days, in a dystopian future. England is barren, food is short, the land is barren, oil has run out, and violence is imminent. But instead of focusing on some poor guttersnipe, Craze's protagonist is no one less than a princess, Princess Eliza Windsor. When the Tudor army, a faction of anti-royalists and discontents storm the palace, Eliza's father is killed and her siblings captured. Only Eliza manages to escape into the terrifying streets of Lond</span>
  <span id="freeText5732395905757136378" style="display:none">Galaxy Craze's new YA is set, like many YA these days, in a dystopian future. England is barren, food is short, the land is barren, oil has run out, and violence is imminent. But instead of focusing on some poor guttersnipe, Craze's protagonist is no one less than a princess, Princess Eliza Windsor. When the Tudor army, a faction of anti-royalists and discontents storm the palace, Eliza's father is killed and her siblings captured. Only Eliza manages to escape into the terrifying streets of London. Thus begins Eliza's mission to save her siblings and restore the crown. The shortages are glossed over, as is the general situation of the country, and, indeed, the world as a whole. Eliza's love interest falls into the story right on cue- and most readers will guess his larger importance in the overall plot. However, dystopian fans may find this an enjoyable read, especially as it features a complete story arc and doesn't leave readers hanging on the edge of a cliff. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5732395905757136378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1411789453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1411789453" />
    <a title="Kayla Edwards" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24780999-kayla-edwards"><img alt="Kayla Edwards" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411656250p2/24780999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1411789453?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla Edwards" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla Edwards" href="/user/show/24780999-kayla-edwards">Kayla Edwards</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1411789453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6362627931147675757">I really enjoyed this really unique dystopian novel based on the British monarchy. It was action-packed, kept my attention, and even threw in a little romance. I was pulling for Eliza and really got caught up in her struggle. I appreciated the fact that the author did not conveniently allow our heroine to escape unscathed. It makes the story more real and believable. My only problem with the novel was the ending. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[If you want a happy, wrap-it-all-up ending - do it. If you don't, do</span></span>
  <span id="freeText6362627931147675757" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this really unique dystopian novel based on the British monarchy. It was action-packed, kept my attention, and even threw in a little romance. I was pulling for Eliza and really got caught up in her struggle. I appreciated the fact that the author did not conveniently allow our heroine to escape unscathed. It makes the story more real and believable. My only problem with the novel was the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[If you want a happy, wrap-it-all-up ending - do it. If you don't, don't do it. I really didn't like that the author did both here. It just felt sloppy to me, as though she wanted an "out" just in case she decided to write a sequel. Everything is nicely wrapped up and settled in an epilogue and then BAM! The last line or so brings in a mysterious new character never previously alluded to and reintroduces a weapon from the beginning of the book. It just read as gimicky to me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But aside from the ending, I really enjoyed this novel and it was a quick read.</span>

<div id="review_358085496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358085496" />
    <a title="Denae Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/857888-denae-christine"><img alt="Denae Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446784625p2/857888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358085496?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denae Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denae Christine" href="/user/show/857888-denae-christine">Denae Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/857888-denae-christine?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer358085496&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358085496" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5948252039439440569">I read this book in one day. That being said, it was not because the book was so good but because I was forcing myself to keep picking it up. This book was a very quick and easy read. Lots happened, and there weren't any slow scenes.<br/>How do I explain this book?<br/><br/>Characters.<br/>They held little interest for me, never fleshed out and not very different to each other. They kept making unbelievably stupid decisions (more about this in a bit), and I could not force myself to care if they died. At the final </span>
  <span id="freeText5948252039439440569" style="display:none">I read this book in one day. That being said, it was not because the book was so good but because I was forcing myself to keep picking it up. This book was a very quick and easy read. Lots happened, and there weren't any slow scenes.<br />How do I explain this book?<br /><br />Characters.<br />They held little interest for me, never fleshed out and not very different to each other. They kept making unbelievably stupid decisions (more about this in a bit), and I could not force myself to care if they died. At the final battle, I was literally laughing as I summarized the fighting for my indifferent sister.<br /><br />Romance.<br />Very abrupt and also unbelievable. Will saves her life (2 or 3 times), and she watches him constantly, then, suddenly, when they are alone having dinner together they start kissing. ?? Nothing discussed beforehand. Then they sleep NEXT to each other. These two have been enemies (well, pretend enemies anyway), and they hardly know each other. Bah.<br /><br />Plot/actions.<br />Again, unbelievable. I can swallow the "magic and dragons and aliens" sort of unbelievable, but not this. Maybe I really want to say, "illogical". I shall name the incidents I bothered keeping track of. Believe me, there were plenty more.<br />First, Eliza and her brother are in the woods, standing on the ground next to their horses when they hear the approach of some Roamers (armed cannibals). There's no time! They duck under a rock outcropping and shoo away the horses just in the nick of time. Phew. The Roamers walk right past them, and they are safe. WHY didn't they just jump on their horses (I'm sure it takes less time to get in a saddle than it does to hide under a rocky outcropping) and gallop away?<br />Second, she's dancing with her father when Hollister's men ride into the ballroom (how they got horses into the ballroom I don't know) and start shooting at the guests. Hollister points his gun at Eliza's chest (very close, no chance of missing) and pulls back the hammer, but then her father shoves her out of the way and is shot instead (OK, I guess that could happen). She starts weeping over her father's death. Then her sister is suddenly there and pulling her up the stairs away from the ballroom. Um, what happened to Hollister? He had a gun, and two of the three people he came to shoot were within his sights, and he just lets them get away? Hmm.<br />Third, the Princesses and Prince are in Jaimie's room when Hollister's goons storm in. There's a secret dumbwaiter in the closet, but only Eliza is hidden in the closet when the goons show up. Oh, no, there's no time for her to climb into the dumbwaiter (which is big enough for all three siblings), and so she tucks herself into a dark corner of the closet and hopes to go unnoticed. ?? She is mere inches from safety, but decides she doesn't have time and goes with just HOPING she won't be seen? GC should have had the dumbwaiter get stuck (it IS rather old) if she really wanted Eliza to be seen.<br />Next, these super poor homeless people give her some warm clothes for free. Maybe they were just being nice, but they didn't even have good clothes for themselves.<br />Next, she arrives at the army camp, and the first man she meets tries to take advantage of her. Right in the middle of the camp. Obviously she screams and Portia, an officer, comes out to banish the man.<br />Next, Portia turns out to be a horrible young woman who picks on Eliza for no apparent reason. Portia is supposed to be an officer, and this army is supposed to be organized and well armed. Portia cuts off Eliza's hair and burns a mark onto her face. Eliza tries running away, but is caught and sentenced to die. Even though she joined the army of her own free will.<br />Next, she finds her siblings in a cell in the castle (no one having recognized her). Then a guard appears and Eliza runs. Why? She was pretending to be a new servant and didn't even try to bluff her way out of that one. Then she somehow gets trapped on the roof (although, since she has lived in that castle, you would think she would know her way around better) and has to jump into the moat. The moat has snakes, but she somehow avoids getting bitten.<br />Next, she's going to be sent to Wales, but she hears her siblings are going to be executed within the week. So, she gathers a ragtag bunch of farmers and sets off. At every village, the group grows. Even though, supposedly, Hollister had conscripted or killed most of the English. And Eliza doesn't even question all these random people joining her army, although they could easily be enemy infiltrators. (At one point, a dark bearded man brings some troops which doubles her army, and she doesn't even bat an eye, although I thought it was very suspicious.)<br />Next, their first battle they win because all the bad guys were caught sleeping. Oops.<br />Next, the final battle was chaotic and I have no clue how the good guys won that one. At one point, Will and his father are wrestling over the hangman's lever, and Will drops his sword. Oh, no! Jaimie, the six-year-old, dashes out, grabs the dropped sword, circles behind Will's father, and throws the sword to Will, who catches it and disarms his father in one move.<br />AND there were more, but I won't bother to list them all.<br /><br />Random coincidences.<br />I once read/heard that coincidences to get your character into trouble are great, but coincidences to get your character out of trouble are lazy. There were WAY too many of the latter in this book. Oh, look, the pet bird happened to survive. The characters kept accomplishing something just in time. Will happened to be in the right place at the right time about 8 times. Her locket happened to make its way back to her. Caligua happened to find her to help Eliza, twice. They happened to show up just in time to stop the hanging.<br /><br />So, lots and lots of stuff happened, it just wasn't very well put together.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5948252039439440569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_234199173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234199173" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3388215-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373331875p2/3388215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234199173?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/3388215-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234199173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6944164077880439097">THE LAST PRINCESS had been on my radar for awhile. Why? Because I LOVE me some royal family gossip – any royal family. And obviously I love science fiction, the apocalypse, and things that seem like THE POSTMAN until Kevin Costner went and ruined it all. On paper, THE LAST PRINCESS by Galaxy Craze seems like the perfect mixture of this, but there was something about the story that kind of disappointed me. It might have been the length (way too short)… Actually, it was probably the length.<br/><br/>Followi</span>
  <span id="freeText6944164077880439097" style="display:none">THE LAST PRINCESS had been on my radar for awhile. Why? Because I LOVE me some royal family gossip – any royal family. And obviously I love science fiction, the apocalypse, and things that seem like THE POSTMAN until Kevin Costner went and ruined it all. On paper, THE LAST PRINCESS by Galaxy Craze seems like the perfect mixture of this, but there was something about the story that kind of disappointed me. It might have been the length (way too short)… Actually, it was probably the length.<br /><br />Following Princess Eliza, THE LAST PRINCESS chronicles the life of a girl second in line to the throne of England after the destruction of the world as we know it in the Seventeen Days, a not-very-well explained but very-well-described event. The sky rained fire and acid rain, animals died, the world went silent, and the UK was left alone. Eliza’s mother was assassinated, and the rise of the New Guard has left the royal family on edge, until one fateful ball starts events spinning that will change the UK forever…<br /><br />The idea behind this book is wonderful, mostly unique, and totally took me back to THE POSTMAN. In THE LAST PRINCESS, we find Eliza doing battle with the New Guard, an organization led by a brutal man and his bloodthirsty army trying to conquer the UK and replace the Windsor line with their regime. Except their regime is pretty much worse than the one in place whose only sin is having nice parties and a little more food. But let’s face it – if this ever happened, I expect 95% of rich people/royals/politicians to be hoarding food waiting for us poor people to starve to death. And this Cornelius Hollister guy seems like he’d be so much worse.<br /><br />I think I just rambled off there. Anyway…<br /><br />After an attack on a royal ball leaves the family broken and Eliza running for her life, the real action begins. We begin to crack this vivid post-apocalyptic world and delve into a story that is focused heavily on the action. There is a romantic element, but if you are a fan of kicking butt and adventuring, this story will definitely appeal to you. The romance in this one wasn’t needed, and in fact I felt like the author added it for two reasons – 1.) the notion that all YA books need romance and 2.) the inevitable twist. But I didn’t buy the twists related to our dear designated love interest, who wasn’t developed nearly as much as I had hoped.<br /><br />But where we had flat secondary characters, I quite enjoyed Eliza. I am not always a big fan of teenage characters who act like whiney spoiled sixteen year old brats, maybe because at heart I might be 10 but in body I am quite a bit older than that. Eliza was every bit the calm, collected, and cultured young lady she should have been, being a Princess and all. Was she foolish? Yes. Did she make really stupid decisions? Yes. But I can’t fault this book based on the fact that the main character was desperate to save her family. In the same boat, I know I would probably have done the same thing.<br /><br />World building isn’t totally impressive. Why? The Seventeen Days is never explained in depth. We know what happened, but never why. Likewise, the facts about the aftereffects aren’t really acknowledged. I wish we could have known more about this. We’ve got dead birds, seas that crush sailing ships, and dead trees, but how in the world did we manage to have complete desertion and overgrowth between Hampton Court Palace and the Tower of London where a horse could easily pass unnoticed? Also, did Eliza’s horse really manage to get from the Tower of London to Balmoral Castle THAT quickly? It’s over 600 miles and it’s implied that she got there in two or three days while she was badly injured.<br /><br />This book heavily borrows tropes from the post-apocalyptic genre. Once again, I won’t call it dystopian because it isn’t really – there is nothing seemingly perfect about this world, not a fatal flaw that cracks the system. But we do have a politically-minded post-apocalyptic story laden with action, adventure, war, family drama, and just a smidge of romance. But the story fails on one issue – the book is too damn short and everything glossed over. I wanted more, and instead I got a rushed conclusion where things suddenly jumped forward days at a time with no explanation, no power, no real basis.<br /><br />World Building - ♥♥♥<br />World is not fully explained, but vividly described. Eliza constantly thinks Balmoral is in England, which should theoretically make the Scottish people angry.<br /><br />Characterization - ♥♥<br />Only Eliza is ever fleshed out, and a lot of her characterization relies on predictable tropes.<br /><br />The Love Factor - ♥♥<br />Girl and designated love interest have googly eyes almost immediately resulting in instalove; boy inexplicably drawn to girl; pair is making out after knowing each other very briefly; romance is very secondary to rest of plot<br /><br />Assorted WTFery - ♥♥♥<br />Who could possibly think Cornelius Hollister was better than the King? Brutal dictator inspires army of hooligans to basically pillage the country. Don’t see how this would go over well.<br /><br />VERDICT: Belayed by some shoddy explanations and a length that is WAY too short for the material needing to be covered, THE LAST PRINCESS is still a very interesting entry into the post-apocalyptic market – but could have been so much more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6944164077880439097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_322134618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322134618" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6322695-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401352517p2/6322695.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322134618?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/6322695-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322134618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2280790940203400540">The Last Princess by Galaxy Craze<br/><br/>I should probably start off by saying that as of this moment, I’m no longer speaking to my mother. What was she thinking naming me Jessica when she could have named me Galaxy. I can honestly state that my biggest motivation for buying this book, initially, was because it seemed incredibly cool to have a book by someone named ‘Galaxy Craze’ on my bookshelf. I’m being serious, too. <br/><br/>There’s more, of course, to <i>The Last Princess</i> than just the author’s completely awes</span>
  <span id="freeText2280790940203400540" style="display:none">The Last Princess by Galaxy Craze<br /><br />I should probably start off by saying that as of this moment, I’m no longer speaking to my mother. What was she thinking naming me Jessica when she could have named me Galaxy. I can honestly state that my biggest motivation for buying this book, initially, was because it seemed incredibly cool to have a book by someone named ‘Galaxy Craze’ on my bookshelf. I’m being serious, too. <br /><br />There’s more, of course, to <i>The Last Princess</i> than just the author’s completely awesome name. <br /><br />Taking place several years into the future, the book is told from the point of view of Eliza, a princess of England. The England we know is replaced by a disaster ridden, darker world after a series of natural disasters decimates the world. <br /><br />Following the usual pattern of dystopian YA fiction, things are tough. Food is luxury and there people out there who are willing to do, and eat, anything to survive. <br /><br />If things weren’t bad enough, someone out there is trying to overthrow the crown! After a violent attack on the palace, sixteen year old Eliza is the only royal that manages to escape.<br /><br />Determined to exact revenge on the man who killed her family, Eliza joins the enemy forces, in disguise. There, she meets a person who hands her back the hope she’s lost…<br /><br />I sort of have mixed feelings about this book. As a rule, I try not to give too harsh of reviews, mainly because I don’t really feel like it’s my job to rip apart something that someone actually put something into. As a whole, <i>The Last Princess</i> wasn’t a bad book. In fact, it was a decent read. I didn’t have to force my way through it, which is usually a good sign. <br /><br />The good things about <i>The Last Princess</i><br /><br />It has a really interesting plot. It was nice to see a dystopian novel taking place somewhere other than America. In a way, the entire thought process was different, which intrigued me. <br /><br />I honestly liked the characters. Eliza was a good character, strong. Despite being slightly confused at her pathway to doing what she had to do to get what she needed done, I found her quite enjoyable.<br />The length. Normally, I don’t mind long books. But with the plot of this book, I’m glad it ended swiftly, rather than dragging it out.<br /><br />The bad things about <i>The Last Princess</i><br /><br />The Characters.<br /><br />In general, I liked Eliza and Wesley. The biggest problem I had with them was that I felt like despite them being the main characters in the story, they weren’t well rounded. I sort of felt like the characters were holding back the entire time, hiding something of themselves that was vital to the telling of the story.<br /><br />A lot was left unexplained. During parts of the story, I found myself wondering things like, “why do the people in the woods eat people? Did they just wake up one day and decide to start hunting humans, or was it something like a ‘I had no other choice, I was starving to death and he was dying’ sort of thing” or “what made Wesley want to do this? What’s his motivation?” As a person who firmly believes that characters drive the story, I was slightly disappointed that the some of the characters didn’t really have a lot of leg to stand on.<br /><br />The story itself was a little bit lacking. Not in a so bad I couldn’t read it way, but sometimes it moved to fast. Things happened that didn’t make sense, decisions made without any real explanation as to why it’s a good decision to be made. A lot of moments in the stories, like Eliza joining the enemy forces seemed so planned, not a quick decision made by a desperate girl who’s just lost her family and is out for revenge against the people who took them away.<br /><br />The fluidity of the book hit a couple rough patches at times, but overall, it wasn’t so horrible. <br /><br />The worst part, I think, is that there will be a sequel. Maybe it’s just me. I’m going through a stage when I wish I could find a decent YA book that doesn’t have a sequel to it. In a way, despite what I didn’t like about it, it seemed like a whole story. It had a beginning, middle, and end. I don’t see a reason to keep going.<br /><br />In conclusion, if you are looking for a quick read, then this definitely the book for you. It’s cute, in a fun way, but nothing epic (in the land of dystopia, where a book like <i>the hunger games</i> are leading the pack in the awesome department, I honestly believe that it’s a lot to live up to).<br /><br />3 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2280790940203400540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sXIExKEM4mAF6m9wx8+ECMHUm5jR20ibZCntZwJr5cUI0JJwpJ5nmy5XcVgaAPwM9hnr/MOevJRFmZUAYT0DLg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cPG2VefhMTiSO/4GA7mDMDqRCHz8/Ine7Gy7aMixKaTJUyDh4nO0w7mG4C7edvs0DVx4GO65fdHN3MMPq+fPTw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer3611674684214855008">Galaxy Craze (born 1972 in London, England) is an actress and writer. She moved to the U.S. with her mother in 1980 and currently lives in Brooklyn, NY. She appeared in a few independent films in the late 1990s, and wrote a novel, <i>By the Shore</i>, published in 1999. She is a 1993 graduate of Barnard College.<br/><br/>Craze told an interviewer that she "didn't say I wanted to be a writer, I just knew that's wha</span>
  <span id="freeText3611674684214855008" style="display:none">Galaxy Craze (born 1972 in London, England) is an actress and writer. She moved to the U.S. with her mother in 1980 and currently lives in Brooklyn, NY. She appeared in a few independent films in the late 1990s, and wrote a novel, <i>By the Shore</i>, published in 1999. She is a 1993 graduate of Barnard College.<br /><br />Craze told an interviewer that she "didn't say I wanted to be a writer, I just knew that's what I like to do." Another interviewer described her "beauty (as) a quiet, dreamy, and ethereal sort."<br /></span>
